## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The target variable dP_dt is the instantaneous population growth rate, given time t and current population P. This is a classic population dynamics modeling task where the rate of change of a population is expressed as a function of its current size and possibly time, reflecting density-dependent regulation, exponential growth, or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth proportional to current population)
- Logistic growth (quadratic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (or dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)) (self-limiting growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric density dependence, often used for tumor or population growth with decelerating rate)
- Generalized logistic (theta-logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence scaling)
- Allee effect (cubic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (population growth with positive density dependence at low numbers)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (environmental forcing making per-capita growth increase/decrease over time)
- Periodic forcing on growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (seasonal or periodic environmental fluctuation)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (linear change in carrying capacity over time, e.g., habitat restoration or degradation)
- Density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (c2 + P) (Michaelis-Menten-type mortality with saturating predator or resource limitation)
- Beverton-Holt recruitment: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + P) - c2 * P (discrete-time stock-recruitment translated to continuous form)
- Ricker-like growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth and linear death, often in fisheries)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2 (flexible asymmetric sigmoid growth, with shape parameter c2)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density‑dependent regulation → growth rate decreases as P increases, often captured by terms like -c1*P**2 or -c1*P/(c2+P)
- Positive density dependence at low numbers (Allee effect) → growth rate increases for small P, modelled by factors (P - c) < 0 giving negative growth for very small populations
- Environmental seasonality → explicit periodic dependence on t, e.g., sin(c*t), creating oscillations in dP/dt
- Long‑term habitat change → carrying capacity or per‑capita growth parameters as linear or exponential functions of t
- Decelerating growth without explicit carrying capacity → log(P) dependence (Gompertz) or exponential saturation (Ricker), producing asymmetric growth curves
- Saturating mortality/consumption → rational functions of P (Michaelis‑Menten form) reducing per‑capita growth rate at high densities
- Regime shifts / threshold population → piecewise or switching functions where growth rate changes abruptly at a critical P (e.g., harvesting threshold or extinction threshold)

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG14)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P + c6*P*exp(-c7*t)
Candidates evaluated: 68

The Ground Truth (GT) function is:
\[
c_0\left(1 - \frac{P}{c_2}\right)P + c_3\left(1 - e^{-c_5 P}\right)P + c_6 P e^{-c_7 t}
\]
with given constants. Expanding:
\[
-\frac{c_0}{c_2}P^2 + (c_0+c_3)P - c_3Pe^{-c_5 P} + c_6Pe^{-c_7 t}
\]
This is a sum of exactly four basis functions: \(P^2\), \(P\), \(Pe^{aP}\), and \(Pe^{bt}\) (with \(a=-c_5\), \(b=-c_7\)).

**Candidate 1:**
\[
P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 e^{P c_3} + P c_4 e^{c_5 t} + c_6 \sin(c_7 t + c_8) + c_9
\]
By assigning \(c_6 = 0\) and \(c_9 = 0\), the extra sine and constant terms vanish completely, yielding:
\[
P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 e^{P c_3} + P c_4 e^{c_5 t}
\]
Since all candidate constants are free, we can match the GT exactly:
- \(c_0 \rightarrow -\frac{c_{0,GT}}{c_{2,GT}}\)
- \(c_1 \rightarrow c_{0,GT} + c_{3,GT}\)
- \(c_2 \rightarrow -c_{3,GT}\), \(c_3 \rightarrow -c_{5,GT}\)
- \(c_4 \rightarrow c_{6,GT}\), \(c_5 \rightarrow -c_{7,GT}\)

No algebraic contradictions arise, and the domain allows non‑negative \(P, t\) (absolute values are not involved). Therefore Candidate 1 is mathematically equivalent to the GT.

Other candidates were reviewed, but the presence of a valid match makes them irrelevant for the final verdict.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and determine which candidates can match it exactly.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.11424*(1 - P/40.698)*P + 0.11424*(1 - exp(-0.08368*P))*P + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `0.11424*P - 0.11424*P²/40.698` = `0.11424*P - 0.002807*P²`
- Second term: `0.11424*P - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P)`
- Third term: `0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)`

Combining:
```
GT = -0.002807*P² + 0.22848*P - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P) + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

This has the form:
```
GT = a*P² + b*P + c*P*exp(d*P) + e*P*exp(f*t)
```

where `a < 0`, `d < 0` (negative exponent in P), and `f < 0` (negative exponent in t).

So the GT structure is: **P²·(const) + P·(const) + P·exp(negative·P)·(const) + P·exp(negative·t)·(const)**

Now let me check each candidate against this structure.

The key structural requirement is:
1. A `P²` term
2. A `P` term  
3. A `P*exp(c*P)` term
4. A `P*exp(c*t)` term
5. No other independent basis functions

Any candidate that has exactly these four basis functions (possibly with additional terms that can be zeroed out or absorbed) can match.
